  <raw>Ole Miss football coach had many happy investments, returns



Ole Miss Athletic Director Pete Boone is a former banker familiar with the bottom line.
He admitted Wednesday that his previous line of work had taught him to appreciate the bottom line, but understand the nature of what it consisted of.
In a fiscal evaluation, the coaching tenure of David Cutcliffe brought many happy returns. Bouyed by the play of Eli Manning, who committed to Ole Miss largely in part to Cutcliffe's work with older brother Peyton at Tennessee, the Rebels' on-the-field success helped spur off-the-field growth for the University of Mississippi's athletic program.

During Cutcliffe's tenure at Ole Miss Vaught-Hemingway Stadium underwent a multi-milllion dollar renovation to add almost 20,000 new seats and an entire new luxury box seating area for alumni and boosters.
Even more so than the additions to Vaught-Hemingway, the expansion jewel for Ole Miss came just months ago, as the Indoor Practice Facility was finally completed after two years and close to $100 million in construction. The state-of-the-art facility houses modern equipment, including a game-sized indoor practice field.
But just any business grows, so too do problems. As the Rebels became a national name in college football under Cutcliffe and Manning, disciplinary issues emerged as well. Just this season as many as five players faced criminal charges ranging from felony reckless endangerment to aggravated assault to rape.
In addition to maintaining a case-by-case approach to criminal matters with players, Cutcliffe drew fire for player dismissals and suspensions without public explanation. In 2004, two players were dismissed and countless disciplined with little more than the explanation of a "team rules violation" from the team.
Nevertheless, Cutcliffe maintained a steady graduation rate among players and a bevvy of Academic All-Americans. Cutcliffe was said to be a model of integrity, something Khayat said Wednesday that Cutcliffe's coaching exemplified.
Just days before Cutcliffe began talks with Boone, a bronze statue was raised in All-American Plaza, connecting the stadium renovations with the IPF. None of it existed before Cutcliffe's tenure at Ole Miss.
(C) 2003 Daily Mississippian via U-WIRE</raw>
